GEOLOGIC SUMMARY & ZONES OF INTEREST
NEWFIELD PRODUCTION COMPANY
ROLFSRUD STATE 152-96-29-32-13HLW
SESE SECTION 20-T152N-R96W
McKENZIE COUNTY, NORTH DAKOTA

GENERAL OVERVIEW:

On August 20, 2014, Newfield Production Company's Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW was
"spudded" as a doublelateral well, targeting oil production out of the TRFKU (TF1) facies of the Three
Forks Formation. The subject well was drilled in the Westburg, located approximately 3 miles North, 3
miles West of Keene, in McKenzie County, North Dakota. Keene located in the central portion of the
Williston Basin. Surface location of the Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW is located at 370' FSL, 828'
FEL, SESE Section 20T152NR96W. Horizontal wellpath for the Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW
was planned to follow a structure to the south along a proposed azimuth of 176.24° with an estimated
89.5° formation dip to a total depth of 21192'

OFFSET INFORAMATION:

The main offset wells used for drilling Newfield Production Company's Rolfsrud State 1529629
3213HLW was the Rolfsrud State 15296293210H. Newfield Production Company drilled the Rolfsrud
State 15296293213HLW in September of 2014, API number of 33053061930000. Other offsets
include the State of ND E1 and Rolfsrud Unit 1.

ENGINEERING:

Newfield Production Company's Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW was drilled with Patterson
UTI drill rig #335. Pad height of the Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW was 2,349.6' above mean sea
level with a KB height located at 2,374.6' above mean sea level, 25' above ground level.

The Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW was drilled with fresh water from surface to 1,713'. A
switch was then made, and oil base drill mud was used from 1,713' to 11,352'. Once horizontal, salt
brine was used from 11,352' to total depth at 21,192'.

The Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW was initially drilled as a 13 ½" hole to 1,713' MD, then 9
5/8" 36# J55 LTC casing was set to a depth of 1,713' through the Fox Hills Formation. The Rolfsrud
State 15296293213HLW then progressed as an 8 ¾" hole from the base of the Fox Hills Formation
until the KOP in the Lodgepole Formation at 10,050' MD. At KOP a trip was made for to pick up a
directional assembly, Directional work from here was performed by Steve Topinka, Doug Balou and
Dustin Yost from Baker Hughes Inteq. The curve was then built at a rate of 10.1° / 100', landing
horizontal on August 28th 2014 at 11,352' MD (10,616.72' TVD). Once landed 7" 29# L80HP BTC
intermediate casing was set to a depth of 11,342' then cemented. Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW
then progressed to a total depth 21192'. Two trips were made in the lateral for MWD tools. The second
trip revealed two jets that were plugged on bit #6. Total depth was reached on September 9th, 2014
with a bottom hole location of 253.44' FSL, 122.67' FEL SESE Section 32T150NR99W. Upon total depth
a 4 ½" 5" 18# P110 tapered liner was ran to a depth of 21,192' MD with fracture stimulation planned to
enhance the well. (see attached daily drilling summary)

The Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW was completed with (6) six drill bits and took a total of
212.5 hours to complete, for an average penetration rate of 101 ft/hr (see attached bit record summary
and drilling parameter charts).

GEOLOGICAL EVALUATION:

Geologic supervision of Newfield Production Company's Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW
well was provided by GeoLink Geological Services with twoman geosteering and geological consulting
service. Geologic evaluation began at a measured depth of 8,000' MD in the Kibbey Formation and
continued to a total depth of 21,192' at the end of the lateral. Two gas analyzers were utilized during
GEOLOGIC SUMMARY & ZONES OF INTEREST
NEWFIELD PRODUCTION COMPANY
ROLFSRUD STATE 152-96-29-32-13HLW
SESE SECTION 20-T152N-R96W
McKENZIE COUNTY, NORTH DAKOTA

the Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW: a Pason IR Gas Chromatograph overseen by Pason Systems and
a MSI Blue Box overseen by GeoLink Geological Services. Both detectors were used to record gas levels
at the rigs shakers during the vertical, curve and horizontal portions of the well and were integrated into
Pason System's electronic drilling recorder (EDR). Gamma data was provided by Baker Hughes Inteq.
Gas, Gamma and ROP data were then integrated into Mudlogging System's MPlot software and into
Stoner Engineering's SES3 geosteering software for evaluation. Lagged samples were also taken and
logged into Mudlogging System's MPlot. Once logging depth was reached at 8,000' within the Kibbey
formation, 30' samples were taken until landing horizontal in the Three Forks at 11,352' MD. 50'
samples were taken upon landing in the Three Forks until total depth at 21,192' MD. Cuttings were then
cleaned of drilling fluids and analyzed under both a binocular microscope and an UV fluoroscope.
Cuttings were tested with acid and Alizarin red to distinguish between carbonates. Naphthalene and
Acetone were used to examine oil cut from within the cuttings. Sample descriptions were then added
into the mudlogs along with a photo for record. After sample evaluation, one set of dry cuttings were
saved, packaged and mailed into the State of North Dakota.

Horizontal well path of the Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW had a below average in zone
percentage, mostly due to getting low at 17,200' into the dolomitic claystone below the target zone, and
caught below a hard streak. Slides up were not yielding because of the hard streak and two jets on bit #6

were plugged, which was later observed with a trip. 100% of the production well bore was drilled within
the Three Forks. 65.7% drilled within the productive TF1 (TRFKU) rock of the Three Forks Formation.
14% was drilled within the productive TRFKU B facies rock of the Three Forks. 20.3% was drilled within
the productive A facies rock of the Three Forks formation. 65.7% was drilled within the 15' target
window. This was due to variations in dip and the inability to control the wellbore from drastic
deflections. Formation dip at the start of the lateral showed a down dip of an 89.48° from 10,866'MD to
13,093' MD, dropping 22' of TVD. Dip then began to roll over to 89.25° from 13,093' MD to 15,108' MD,
dropping 26' of TVD. Between 15,108'MD and 18,580' MD dip flattened to an average of an 89.85° only
dropping a total of 3'. From here until TD dip steepened to an 89.5° dropping a total of 7' of TVD.
Average regional formation dip for the lateral was an 89.58°, showing a net 75' drop over the 10,688' of
lateral. Lateral profile while drilling the Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW is summarized in the

Three Fork samples from the lateral portion of the well showed fair to moderate oil shows from
throughout the zones drilled. Sample fluorescence ranged between spotty yellow to even pale yellow
which correlates to 3140 API gravity, light crude, with specific gravity's in the range of 0.87 ­ 0.83. Fair
oil stain was seen during sample evaluation within the Three Forks with samples exhibiting even light
brown oil stains. Average Three Fork samples produced bright to semi bright milky white to blue white
cut fluorescence when tested with Acetone under the UV fluoroscope. Fair to tight visible crystalline
porosity was observed in Three Fork samples when viewed under the binocular microscope. Three Fork
samples all exhibited faint to moderate hydrocarbon odors in preparation for sample evaluation. Traces
of free oil could be seen while washing most samples. Sample evaluation combined with gas and oil
shows point to the Rolfsrud State 15296293213HLW being a commercially viable, productive oil well.

Thank you for the opportunity to serve as Newfield Production Company's well site geologist on this
well. If you have any questions, please feel free to contact us at GeoLink, Inc.

Dear Sarah:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24863, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is granted on
the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement shall be located approximately down the north-south axis (500'
drilling corridor, per Commission policy) and not closer than 200 feet to the north or south boundary within the 2560 acre spacing unit
consisting of Sections 28, 29, 32 & 33 T152N R96W. Tool error need not be considered except when deemed necessary by the Director.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock disposal must
be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and
flow-back whenever filtration operations are conducted. Due to drainage adjacent to the well site, a dike is required
surrounding the entire location. NEWFIELD PRODUCTION COMPANY must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28
(Safety Regulation) when contemplating simultaneous operations on the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-
03-28 (Safety Regulation) "No boiler, portable electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than 150 feet to any
producing well or oil tank." NEWFIELD PROD CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Joyce Kohut at 701-202-1288 prior to
location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and completion
operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of the land surface and
freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized
representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director
prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The proposed directional
plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing point is: 570'S and 4433'E. Also, based on the
azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10718'S and 943'E.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved drilling permit
on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd business day following
publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn
affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and
any other information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit,
the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given immediately upon the
spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information
must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding.
Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Sarah King
August 15, 2014
Page 2
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall file a certified
copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or
in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the
survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one
adobe document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when sliding) and 90
feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby granted. Such
information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records wherever located.
Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the Director and his representatives to come
upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and
operation of such wells and to have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The
information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission and
its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail cement
utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and porosity zones
can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and (3) a log from which the
presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation log) in every well in which production
or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as
one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a
standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

3. Casing and cementing will be done to protect potentially productive
hydrocarbons, fresh water zones, abnormal pressure zones,
and prospectively valuable mineral deposits.
A. Casing head: 9 5/8" SOW x 11" 5M multi-bowl tested to 5000 psi
Tubing head 11" 5M x 7 1/16" 10M tested to 5000 psi
B. Operators minimum specifications for pressure control equipment are shown on the attached BOP
schematic.
After running 9 5/8" surface casing and prior to drilling out, blind rams, pipe rams, manifold,
upper and lower kelly cock and safety valve will be pressure tested to 5000 psi. Hydril will be tested
to 3500 psi. Thereafter, the BOPE will be checked daily for mechanical operations and will be noted
in the IADC drilling reports. Before and after running 7" intermediate casing the BOPE will be tested
in the same manner. BOP will be tested at low pressure to 250 psi.
Gas Buster will be fully rigged up and tested for fluid integrity, using anti-freeze solution
prior to drilling out 9 5/8" surface casing.

9. NDIC Oil and Gas Notices
a) 72 Hours prior to spud. NDIC @ (701) 328-8020

c) 24 hrs prior to P & A.
d) 24 hrs prior to removing fluid from reserve pit.
10. Deviation & MWD Surveys
9 5/8" surface hole: 3 degrees max inclination & 1 deg/100' max DLS, survey every 500'
9 5/8" casing shoe to KOP: 3 degrees max inclination - adjust KOP as necessary, survey every 100'
KOP to 7" casing shoe: survey every 30'
7" casing shoe to TD: survey every 90', if turning survey every 30'
Gamma- Will be logged from KOP, through build section, and through lateral section.

D. Other Drilling Considerations & Lessons Learned:
1. Gas Buster- Not to be used for venting off flowline. Divert all flow to gas buster.
2. Lateral Drilling- Minimize DLS.
3. Salt Sections: Tight hole and stuck pipe may occur. Control drill +/-5' and back-ream
as necessary. Spot freshwater only if severely stuck.
4. Do not rotate PDC bit inside 7" casing while displacing well with kill weight fluids.
Ensure bit & motor are in open hole section.
5. Transfer OBM from storage tanks to rig tanks over the shaker screens.

To whom it may concern:
This notice is intended to confirm that the proposed completion consisting of hydraulic fracture treatment
on the above mentioned well is in compliance with EPA UIC Program Guidance #84 regarding oil and
gas hydraulic fracturing activities using diesel fuels. Newfield is aware of the EPA guidance and does
not intend to inject "diesel fuels" in any quantity. Newfield has confirmed with its fracturing service
provider that "diesel fuels" are not included in the chemicals injected during fracturing treatment of
Newfield operated wells. The above referenced "diesel fuels" are described below by Chemical Abstract
Service Registry Number (CASRN):
1) 68334-30-5 Primary Name: Fuels, diesel
2) 68476-34-6 Primary Name: Fuels, diesel, No. 2
3) 68476-30-2 Primary Name: Fuel oil No. 2
4) 68476-31-3 Primary Name: Fuel oil, No. 4
5) 8008-20-6 Primary Name: Kerosene
